#if CONFIG_XEN_CTRL_INTERFACE_VERSION == 41100
  #undef XC_WANT_COMPAT_DEVICEMODEL_API
  #define __XEN_TOOLS__
  #include <xendevicemodel.h>
  #include <xenforeignmemory.h>

    xendevicemodel_handle *xd;
    xenforeignmemory_handle *xfmem;

    xd = xendevicemodel_open(0, 0);
    xendevicemodel_pin_memory_cacheattr(xd, 0, 0, 0, 0);

    xfmem = xenforeignmemory_open(0, 0);

   *
   * Also, check if xengnttab_grant_copy_segment_t is defined and
   * grant copy operation is implemented.

  #undef XC_WANT_COMPAT_GNTTAB_API
  #undef XC_WANT_COMPAT_MAP_FOREIGN_API
  #include <xenctrl.h>
  #include <xenstore.h>
  #include <xenevtchn.h>
  #include <xengnttab.h>
  #include <xenforeignmemory.h>

  #if !defined(HVM_MAX_VCPUS)
  # error HVM_MAX_VCPUS not defined
  #endif
  int main(void) {
    xc_interface *xc = NULL;
    xenforeignmemory_handle *xfmem;
    xenevtchn_handle *xe;
    xengnttab_handle *xg;
    xengnttab_grant_copy_segment_t* seg = NULL;

    xs_daemon_open();

    xc = xc_interface_open(0, 0, 0);
    xc_hvm_set_mem_type(0, 0, HVMMEM_ram_ro, 0, 0);
    xc_domain_add_to_physmap(0, 0, XENMAPSPACE_gmfn, 0, 0);
    xc_hvm_inject_msi(xc, 0, 0xf0000000, 0x00000000);
    xc_hvm_create_ioreq_server(xc, 0, HVM_IOREQSRV_BUFIOREQ_ATOMIC, NULL);

    xfmem = xenforeignmemory_open(0, 0);
    xenforeignmemory_map(xfmem, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0);

    xe = xenevtchn_open(0, 0);
    xenevtchn_fd(xe);

    xg = xengnttab_open(0, 0);
    xengnttab_grant_copy(xg, 0, seg);

    return 0;
  }

#elif CONFIG_XEN_CTRL_INTERFACE_VERSION == 40800
  /*
   * If we have stable libs the we don't want the libxc compat
   * layers, regardless of what CFLAGS we may have been given.
   *
   * Also, check if xengnttab_grant_copy_segment_t is defined and
   * grant copy operation is implemented.
   */
  #undef XC_WANT_COMPAT_EVTCHN_API
  #undef XC_WANT_COMPAT_GNTTAB_API
  #undef XC_WANT_COMPAT_MAP_FOREIGN_API
  #include <xenctrl.h>
  #include <xenstore.h>
  #include <xenevtchn.h>
  #include <xengnttab.h>
  #include <xenforeignmemory.h>
  #include <stdint.h>
  #include <xen/hvm/hvm_info_table.h>
  #if !defined(HVM_MAX_VCPUS)
  # error HVM_MAX_VCPUS not defined
  #endif
  int main(void) {
    xc_interface *xc = NULL;
    xenforeignmemory_handle *xfmem;
    xenevtchn_handle *xe;
    xengnttab_handle *xg;
    xengnttab_grant_copy_segment_t* seg = NULL;

    xs_daemon_open();

    xc = xc_interface_open(0, 0, 0);
    xc_hvm_set_mem_type(0, 0, HVMMEM_ram_ro, 0, 0);
    xc_domain_add_to_physmap(0, 0, XENMAPSPACE_gmfn, 0, 0);
    xc_hvm_inject_msi(xc, 0, 0xf0000000, 0x00000000);
    xc_hvm_create_ioreq_server(xc, 0, HVM_IOREQSRV_BUFIOREQ_ATOMIC, NULL);

    xfmem = xenforeignmemory_open(0, 0);
    xenforeignmemory_map(xfmem, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0);

    xe = xenevtchn_open(0, 0);
    xenevtchn_fd(xe);

    xg = xengnttab_open(0, 0);
    xengnttab_grant_copy(xg, 0, seg);

    return 0;
  }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(numa_has_preferred_many) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_numa_has_preferred_many found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_numa_has_preferred_many)
                #error "__builtin_numa_has_preferred_many not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(numa_has_preferred_many)
            __builtin_numa_has_preferred_many;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(pthread_fchdir_np) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_pthread_fchdir_np found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_pthread_fchdir_np)
                #error "__builtin_pthread_fchdir_np not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(pthread_fchdir_np)
            __builtin_pthread_fchdir_np;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
  #ifndef _GNU_SOURCE
  #define _GNU_SOURCE
  #endif

  #include <pthread.h>

  static void *f(void *p) { return NULL; }
  int main(void)
  {
    int setsize = CPU_ALLOC_SIZE(64);
    pthread_t thread;
    cpu_set_t *cpuset;
    pthread_create(&thread, 0, f, 0);
    cpuset = CPU_ALLOC(64);
    CPU_ZERO_S(setsize, cpuset);
    pthread_setaffinity_np(thread, setsize, cpuset);
    pthread_getaffinity_np(thread, setsize, cpuset);
    CPU_FREE(cpuset);
    return 0;
  }
